  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_94d84b3f-bdc0-4e42-a89d-98e1f62897d6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer5090751590781175744">'<i>I took the skull from its evidence bag and gently set it on the stainless steel table. 'Tell me who you are...'</i><br/><br/>Forensic anthropologist Dr David Hunter should be at home in London with the woman he loves. Instead, as a favour to a beleaguered colleague, he's on the remote Hebridean island of Runa to inspect a grisly discovery.<br/><br/>Hunter has witnessed death in many guises, but </span>
  <span id="freeText5090751590781175744" style="display:none">'<i>I took the skull from its evidence bag and gently set it on the stainless steel table. 'Tell me who you are...'</i><br /><br />Forensic anthropologist Dr David Hunter should be at home in London with the woman he loves. Instead, as a favour to a beleaguered colleague, he's on the remote Hebridean island of Runa to inspect a grisly discovery.<br /><br />Hunter has witnessed death in many guises, but even he is shocked by what he finds: a body almost totally incinerated but for the feet and a single hand. Could it be a textbook case of spontaneous human combustion? The local police are certain it's an accidental death but Hunter is not convinced. Examining the scorched remains, he finds the evidence he feared. It's clear to him that this was no accident, this was murder.<br /><br />But as the small, isolated community considers the enormity of Hunter's findings, a catastrophic storm hits the island. The power goes down, communication with the mainland ceases, and then the killing begins in earnest...<br /><br />Exploding in a series of violent acts and shocking twists, this is the compelling new crime thriller from a brilliant British storyteller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5090751590781175744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_543162217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543162217" />
    <a title="Gosia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11238145-gosia"><img alt="Gosia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343122615p2/11238145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543162217?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gosia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gosia" href="/user/show/11238145-gosia">Gosia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543162217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8045493061585956395">After enjoying the hell out of "The Chemistry of Death" I was very eager to start reading the second book about Dr Hunter. And... oh boy. I don't really know where to begin.<br/>The book starts interestingly enough: gruesome murder, interesting location, good ol' Dr Hunter... But then it takes over a hundred pages until something, ANYTHING happens. Some of the characters in the book were so cartoonish I was afraid I might injure my eyes with all the eyerolling. Here's your token single mother with a </span>
  <span id="freeText8045493061585956395" style="display:none">After enjoying the hell out of "The Chemistry of Death" I was very eager to start reading the second book about Dr Hunter. And... oh boy. I don't really know where to begin.<br />The book starts interestingly enough: gruesome murder, interesting location, good ol' Dr Hunter... But then it takes over a hundred pages until something, ANYTHING happens. Some of the characters in the book were so cartoonish I was afraid I might injure my eyes with all the eyerolling. Here's your token single mother with a dark past, there's your incompetent and drunken police officer who is completely oblivious to the most obvious facts, there's your spunky young journalist who "just wants to get to the bottom of things". The only reason we know that the retired detective Brody is "meticulous", is because we are told so about ten times, without actually ever really witnessing it through his actions. Dr Hunter is equally infuriating with his sixth sense telling him multiple times "something doesn't quite add up" but we never really get to find out why until it's too late. Come on, Mr. Beckett, let your readers join in on the fun, let them think a little! And then the plot... oh the plot. Formulaic (albeit entertaining) at first, but then within 50 pages it's plot twist after plot twist after plot twist to the point where it was giving me a major headache. What's even worse, by the time I got to the end of the book I realised I don't even care anymore what happens to Dr. Hunter or, for that matter, who the killer is.<br />I gave the book 3 stars because it's still a kind of entertaining read. The reason I'm so harsh is because my expectations were high after Beckett's first David Hunter book. Sadly, "Written in Bone" wasn't half as entertaining as I wanted it to be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8045493061585956395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352663656?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Li&#39;l Owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Li&#39;l Owl" href="/user/show/48372551-li-l-owl"> Li&#39;l Owl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385340052" href="/book/show/46466.Written_in_Bone">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=series">series</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=medical-examiner-forensic-anthropol">medical-examiner-forensic-anthropol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=mystery-crime-suspense-thriller">mystery-crime-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=uk-author-setting">uk-author-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=scotland-author-setting">scotland-author-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=forensics-forensic-science">forensics-forensic-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=detective-police-procedural-sheriff">detective-police-procedural-sheriff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352663656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14265137545914123457"><b>Creepy! Like tiny hairs buzzing on the back of your neck, creepy!</b><br/><br/><br/><i>"Our lives, and sometimes our deaths, are stories written in bone. It provides a telltale record of injuries, neglect or abuse. But in order to find what was written here, first I had to be able to see it."</i><br/><br/>When a body, burned beyond recognition, is found in an abandoned hut on the island of Runa, the local authorities call forensic pathologist, Dr. David Hunter for help.<br/>At first, David refuses, wanting to continue his journey home.</span>
  <span id="freeText14265137545914123457" style="display:none"><b>Creepy! Like tiny hairs buzzing on the back of your neck, creepy!</b><br /><br /><br /><i>"Our lives, and sometimes our deaths, are stories written in bone. It provides a telltale record of injuries, neglect or abuse. But in order to find what was written here, first I had to be able to see it."</i><br /><br />When a body, burned beyond recognition, is found in an abandoned hut on the island of Runa, the local authorities call forensic pathologist, Dr. David Hunter for help.<br />At first, David refuses, wanting to continue his journey home. He wants nothing to do with it. But David's sense of duty to help the deceased find his or her way home is too much to turn his back on. After all, David will only there to assist the local police in setting the perimeters of sex, approximate age, and, with any luck, the cause of death. Then the case will be turned over to them to carry in whatever direction is necessary. It's only supposed to take a couple of days, then he can return home to his wife. <br />But things don't go that way. <br />Not by a long shot. <br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6499985.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter__2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26024.Simon_Beckett" title="Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon Beckett</a> takes place in the Western Isles, a coastal island chain that's separated from the Scottish mainland. The small, sparcly populated island of Runa is even more isolated which sets the scene perfectly for an eerie, ominous feeling, beginning from the very start and becoming more nightmarish and terrifying as the story goes on. The story has plenty of twists and turns that kept me completely unbalanced throughout, all the way to the startling conclusion. <br /><br />This is the second book in the <i>David Hunter </i> series and I loved it just as much as the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death__David_Hunter___1_" title="The Chemistry of Death (David Hunter, #1) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chemistry of Death</a>. Both books are chilling, with likable characters, a rapid pace, and lots of authentic forensic evidence. I'm a huge fan of factual forensic science and this series has plenty of it! I devoured the story from beginning to end and the disturbing, macabre factor is off the scales! Perfect! <br />I am looking forward to the next book in this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14265137545914123457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436113500?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436113500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10271306746141196755">Beckett returns with a stellar sequel to his opening book, which captured the hearts of readers. When an apparent spontaneous combustion case pops up on the remote Scottish island of Runa, what looks like an open and shut case soon reeks of murder. Before long, a murder spree commences and the small island population begins to wonder who among its own is wielding the knife and setting fire to the victims. With a collection of new small-town characters, Beckett returns with a great new plot as wo</span>
  <span id="freeText10271306746141196755" style="display:none">Beckett returns with a stellar sequel to his opening book, which captured the hearts of readers. When an apparent spontaneous combustion case pops up on the remote Scottish island of Runa, what looks like an open and shut case soon reeks of murder. Before long, a murder spree commences and the small island population begins to wonder who among its own is wielding the knife and setting fire to the victims. With a collection of new small-town characters, Beckett returns with a great new plot as wonderful narrative to bring the story to life. The reader will surely devour this book as they did the opening in the series and scramble for the latter two as well. Absolutely spectacular last 50 pages has the reader picking their jaw off the floor more than once. Mystery at its best!!!!<br /><br />Beckett sets himself up to possibly be the UK's Jefferson Bass. While the books do have a great forensic aspect to them, the level of scientific osteo-based learning is less intense. A strong murder theme with wonderful medical references that keeps the reader hooked, I will not deny. I like the idea of using our main character as one who is parachuted into small-town scenarios, as it keeps the story fresh and rids any wonder about Jessica Fletcher syndrome (wherever you go, murder follows or your small town is repeatedly victim to a killer when you are around)!<br /><br />Kudos Mr. Beckett for a sensational piece of work. Bring on Book #3!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10271306746141196755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8665271281057515846" style="display:none">The story moves along at a fairly leisurely pace for most of the book, then suddenly starts taking off near the end like a rocket with action and surprises galore (not to mention gore). Some of the characters I liked didn't fare too well, but I'll get over it, I think. <br /><br />Much like the first book in the series, it takes place in a small town that makes city living sound ideal.     </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930504399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer147019296494706172">Loved this book! I am pushing this author to the top of my fav. pile. I read his first book some time ago and then I forgot about him! (And I keep records of all the books I read so I don't lose track of where I am in a series and what I thought about each.) But wowser, this was a great one.<br/><br/>David Hunter, a former GP, and now working as a forensic anthroplogist ,is called, sort of last minute, to Runa an island in an outoftheway location off the Scottish coast. (Yep, this is all Scotland we're ta</span>
  <span id="freeText147019296494706172" style="display:none">Loved this book! I am pushing this author to the top of my fav. pile. I read his first book some time ago and then I forgot about him! (And I keep records of all the books I read so I don't lose track of where I am in a series and what I thought about each.) But wowser, this was a great one.<br /><br />David Hunter, a former GP, and now working as a forensic anthroplogist ,is called, sort of last minute, to Runa an island in an outoftheway location off the Scottish coast. (Yep, this is all Scotland we're talking about and I love books set there!) It seems a burned body has been found in an old 1,000 year old croft, or cottage. The entire body has been consumed, except for - wait for it - the two feet and one hand! <br /><br />Let me tell you, I could not read this fast enough. David's a charming and engaging MC; the people he's forced to work with in Runa are mostly NOT. The police sergeant on the island is a miserable curmudgeon; many of the 'locals' are crabby as well. There's a rich guy and his wife who live in a mansion-type home on the island with an intriguing back story, and a few women thrown in here and there. Now David HAS a girlfriend on the mainland, but she's angry cuz he's off on another assignment and not with her. (Trope-trope-trope, but we women often do get like this, so it's a trope based on reality.) Back to story...<br /><br />I can't say much without putting it in spoilers, but everything is great about this book. There's a storm. Communications with the mainland are iffy. There's a bar where everyone hangs out. There's atmosphere and lots of sheep and even two dogs. David gets hurt, then he gets hurt some more and all while doing his forensic shtick. And at the end...<br /><br />It's one of those books with such fantastic - and wholly realistic twists - that I want to read it all over again to see where I missed something.<br /><br />Five outstanding stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="147019296494706172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22224378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9100487179092651223">This book rocketed along, with lots of twists and turns until the very last page. It's a variation of the "and then there were none" theme, with all the characters trapped on a very small island in the Hebrides and no obvious suspects for any of the murders. The hero, a forensic anthropologist, is not quite smart enough to figure things out before we do, but that is part of the wonderfully sustained tension. Now I'm off to find the author's first book!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2833955452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14036423438051194827">As a forensic anthropologist, Dr. David Hunter is reminiscent of Dr. Nikki Alexander of television's "Silent Witness". He frequently gets far too close to suspects and police investigators of the cases he consults on, putting his personal relationships under strain and inevitably leading to dramatic life-or-death confrontations near the conclusion of each book. They are thrillers, after all. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter___2_' title='Written in Bone (David Hunter, #2) by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Written in Bone</a> is the second solid instalment in the Dr. David Hunter series by Beckett and revolves aro</span>
  <span id="freeText14036423438051194827" style="display:none">As a forensic anthropologist, Dr. David Hunter is reminiscent of Dr. Nikki Alexander of television's "Silent Witness". He frequently gets far too close to suspects and police investigators of the cases he consults on, putting his personal relationships under strain and inevitably leading to dramatic life-or-death confrontations near the conclusion of each book. They are thrillers, after all. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter___2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter, #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a> is the second solid instalment in the Dr. David Hunter series by Beckett and revolves around the discovery of burned bones in a remote cottage in the Outer Hebrides. Fans of Anne Cleeves' D.I. Perez (Shetland) series will appreciate the bleak and isolated setting. While the actions of the central character defied realism, this was an entertaining and evocative read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14036423438051194827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_83829284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83829284" />
    <a title="Gerald Sinstadt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3095102-gerald-sinstadt"><img alt="Gerald Sinstadt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272455057p2/3095102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83829284?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerald Sinstadt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerald Sinstadt" href="/user/show/3095102-gerald-sinstadt">Gerald Sinstadt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83829284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16904080157255377738">When Patricia Cornwell embarked on her series of novels about a forensic detective, the territory was fresh and interesting. But disciples have appeared, disinterring the bodies and conducting autopsies but finding little that is original. Simon Beckett is a follower though with a link back to Agatha Christie. <br/><br/>Written in Bone has a self-styled forensic anthropologist for a central character, thus justifying any amount of grisly information about burning bodies. But Dr David Hunter is cut off by </span>
  <span id="freeText16904080157255377738" style="display:none">When Patricia Cornwell embarked on her series of novels about a forensic detective, the territory was fresh and interesting. But disciples have appeared, disinterring the bodies and conducting autopsies but finding little that is original. Simon Beckett is a follower though with a link back to Agatha Christie. <br /><br />Written in Bone has a self-styled forensic anthropologist for a central character, thus justifying any amount of grisly information about burning bodies. But Dr David Hunter is cut off by the weather on a Hebridean island seemingly inhabited only by potential murderers; the corpses pile up, drawing suspicion upon one character after another until each is disposed of. Credit to the author for a labyrinthine plot that knows its way out at the end, but by then many readers will have ceased to care. <br /><br />Time to put away the technical know-how and introduce us to real people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16904080157255377738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158757395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158757395" />
    <a title="Roland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1850691-roland"><img alt="Roland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358425416p2/1850691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158757395?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roland" href="/user/show/1850691-roland">Roland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158757395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5091456531746786005">This reader loved The Chemistry of Death and in Written in Bone the descriptions of the actual finds are no less enthralling. However, it is unacceptable if, in I-narration, a third person in a chapter (i.e. a later report by the I-narrator – anything else would be impossible) fails to see shadows lifting themselves from the dark. This is cheating or oversight – not good writing. The extended ending with twist upon twist, too, is not convincing, just laboured. There is more to say – the constant</span>
  <span id="freeText5091456531746786005" style="display:none">This reader loved The Chemistry of Death and in Written in Bone the descriptions of the actual finds are no less enthralling. However, it is unacceptable if, in I-narration, a third person in a chapter (i.e. a later report by the I-narrator – anything else would be impossible) fails to see shadows lifting themselves from the dark. This is cheating or oversight – not good writing. The extended ending with twist upon twist, too, is not convincing, just laboured. There is more to say – the constant build-up of sexual tension which is never released in any form is, at the end of the day, just another fairly cheap, but impotent, trick. And when did you first find that Brody's meticulousness was mentioned once too often? Long before it was mentioned for the last time, right? Disappointed, but still looking forward to Dr Hunter No. 3 – The Chemistry of Death was that good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5091456531746786005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Every sentence earns its place in the book. Again, the atmosphere is palpable, and the characters well-written and vivid.   <span id="freeText8550499917525450665" style="display:none">Like 'Chemistry of death' before it, I really enjoyed this book. Beckett creates a thrilling murder mystery which keeps you hooked to the last page and trust me, I do mean the last page.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403613445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7523606034495281130">This is the second in the David Hunter series. This time set on an isolated Scottish Island, the tension ratchets up and up with each page. Atmospheric and densely plotted, this is an excellent addition to the series. David Hunter is a forensic anthropologist. He's drawn into the investigation of a bizarre find: the partially burnt body of a young woman in a croft. Stories always work well in remote, isolated communities, and in this novel the island becomes cut off by a terrible storm--no commu</span>
  <span id="freeText7523606034495281130" style="display:none">This is the second in the David Hunter series. This time set on an isolated Scottish Island, the tension ratchets up and up with each page. Atmospheric and densely plotted, this is an excellent addition to the series. David Hunter is a forensic anthropologist. He's drawn into the investigation of a bizarre find: the partially burnt body of a young woman in a croft. Stories always work well in remote, isolated communities, and in this novel the island becomes cut off by a terrible storm--no communication with the mainland at all. When David determines that the body has been murdered, he's virtually on his own, and the body count begins to climb.<br />There's a lot of forensic detail in these books, but it's very well presented, always relevant and never preachy, which some forensic novels can be. I guess the books are gory. I'm possibly not the best judge, but if you don't like reading about dead bodies, how they burn, and other such fascinating details, probably give these a miss, but if you like superbly crafted crime novels with genuinely gripping atmosphere then start with the first and enjoy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7523606034495281130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2222319-jill-hutchinson?shelf=mystery-police-procedural">mystery-police-procedural</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824410919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer30596062934514469">Can you say "cliché"...........this book is full of them. I think the author tried too hard in this story to include every possible writing device available, some of which were used successfully by famous mystery writers but have since fallen out of favor.........an island with a small population cut off from the rest of the world by a gigantic storm, murders galore, cardboard characters who are all suspects, distrust of "outsiders", too many twists in the plot. Get the idea?<br/><br/>Dr. David Hunter, a </span>
  <span id="freeText30596062934514469" style="display:none">Can you say "cliché"...........this book is full of them. I think the author tried too hard in this story to include every possible writing device available, some of which were used successfully by famous mystery writers but have since fallen out of favor.........an island with a small population cut off from the rest of the world by a gigantic storm, murders galore, cardboard characters who are all suspects, distrust of "outsiders", too many twists in the plot. Get the idea?<br /><br />Dr. David Hunter, a forensic anthropologist is called to the Outer Hebrides to determine the cause of death for a body found in an abandoned croft. Murder is not considered but, of course, it is murder. And that is just the beginning of a killing spree. Now slip into the clichés mentioned above and off we go.<br /><br />This is the second book in a series which should be read in order since incidents from the first book play a part in the story. So we don't get a real picture of the main character since it appears that terrible things happened to him in the past. It sounds like I hated this book but I really didn't.....it was good enough to keep my attention but just barely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="30596062934514469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14088255469078432416" style="display:none">Plot line:<br />A murder occurs on a small island in the middle of no where. With technology difficulties from a storm, our hero determines how the victim died and that the murderer is still on the island. If you can look past the tragedy that is the main character, it's a pretty good book. So if you choose to read it, I hope you enjoy it more than I did.</span>

<div id="review_3045178939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3045178939" />
    <a title="Paul Weiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss"><img alt="Paul Weiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453113069p2/51664350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3045178939?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Weiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Weiss" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss">Paul Weiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=medical-thriller">medical-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=anthropology">anthropology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3045178939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16801748403624705074"><b>
  <i>"It's the things you never see coming you have to watch out for."</i>
</b><br/><br/>With <b>WRITTEN IN BONE</b>, a solid sequel to his debut novel <b>THE CHEMISTRY OF DEATH</b>, Author Simon Beckett continues to effectively cash in on his real life anthropological experience working with Bill Bass of Tennessee's world famous Body Farm. Unlike many of his competitors in the crowded medical thriller genre who have concentrated on thrill and suspense at the expense of science and medicine, Beckett writes a solid forensic proce</span>
  <span id="freeText16801748403624705074" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"It's the things you never see coming you have to watch out for."</i>
</b><br /><br />With <b>WRITTEN IN BONE</b>, a solid sequel to his debut novel <b>THE CHEMISTRY OF DEATH</b>, Author Simon Beckett continues to effectively cash in on his real life anthropological experience working with Bill Bass of Tennessee's world famous Body Farm. Unlike many of his competitors in the crowded medical thriller genre who have concentrated on thrill and suspense at the expense of science and medicine, Beckett writes a solid forensic procedural with plenty of interesting details on such minutiae as the rate of decay of human bodies under a variety of conditions, the nature of pre- and post-mortem wounds and the tiny differences between slashing and stabbing wounds and their effects on soft tissue and bones that is superbly balanced with the bloody bits and the actual action. Nor has he forgotten about suspense, twists, turns, red herrings and surprise endings!<br /><br />Forensic anthropologist David Hunter has been dispatched to Runa, a God-forsaken barren spit of land in the remote Outer Hebrides in the frigid Atlantic north of Scotland, to investigate a death so bizarre that the first cause coming to everyone's mind is spontaneous human combustion. When a ferocious Arctic storm eliminates all communication with the mainland and clues finally surface that prove the death was in fact murder, the game, as Sherlock Holmes would have said, was definitely afoot! Hunter, cut off from any possible assistance from his police colleagues in Britain and Scotland, is forced to investigate the murder with the only assistance available on the island - Neil Fraser, an unhappy, angry officer who wants nothing more than to stay under the radar until his retirement quietly drinking his way to oblivion and Andrew Brody, an embittered former investigator who retired to the seclusion of Runa after the mysterious unsolved disappearance of his daughter many years earlier.<br /><br /><b>WRITTEN IN BONE</b> is most definitely NOT a cozy mystery in the style of Agatha Christie. That said, the resemblance to <b>AND THEN THERE WAS NONE</b> is unmistakable as the body count on the foul weather-locked island mounts and the only possible suspects are the remaining inhabitants who are looking over their shoulders with growing fear and suspicion. But no potential reader should get the mistaken impression that I'm suggesting <b>WRITTEN IN BONE</b> is derivative. Absolutely not! The characterization is superb, the relationships are as edgy, angsty and as dark as any thriller available today, the dialogue is natural and credible, the twists and turns are devious and ... oh my goodness ... that ending out of left field will leave every reader with a smile knowing that entry #3 in the David Hunter series is just around the corner.<br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /><br />Paul Weiss<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16801748403624705074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736717466?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn Gardner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn Gardner" href="/user/show/40142810-lynn-gardner">Lynn Gardner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736717466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14862690038427582264">This is the second in the David Hunter series by Beckett, and I loved the first so I wanted to continue the series.<br/><br/>In this one, Hunter is asked to check out some charred remains found in a cabin on a secluded island, Runa. The initial belief is that is was an accidental death - people lighting fires and falling asleep next to them is pretty common in a place where tourists come to camp and hike - but Hunter sees clues that indicate it wasn’t accidental after all. His discovery there leads to mor</span>
  <span id="freeText14862690038427582264" style="display:none">This is the second in the David Hunter series by Beckett, and I loved the first so I wanted to continue the series.<br /><br />In this one, Hunter is asked to check out some charred remains found in a cabin on a secluded island, Runa. The initial belief is that is was an accidental death - people lighting fires and falling asleep next to them is pretty common in a place where tourists come to camp and hike - but Hunter sees clues that indicate it wasn’t accidental after all. His discovery there leads to more murders and more destruction. Who on the island could possible be capable of the murder?<br /><br />This one had the same traits as the first that I loved so much: gruesome murders, interesting facts, and a super twisty ending. Even when I thought I had it figured out, Beckett threw in one more twist, and then another for good measure. I’m in awe of the time and work that must go in to planning these books, and Beckett manages to do it well and produce good work.<br /><br />I definitely recommend Beckett to anyone who likes thrillers/suspense and can handle and a few graphic details.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14862690038427582264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3633057720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16832833033744891279">I didn’t expect this book to be so freaking good. I am really really impressed. I liked everything about this book. Honestly? I had suspicions about who could be a murderer but I didn’t think that there might have been more. All the characters are unique, they have different personalities. It’s amazes me how author plays with the reader. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3KhRQHJ+uB71HNgFxjLFpMh1JC+gA32SaT2CPF36rHAkwrYwaueRWGVgDHDYsIHWl2GhhNJEnd3ZvJXBQR8M8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AkQfxZLFfoYyeHGT/ZQNE80atD1PG79Qtd4LjM2zwsD6Lvi1ilxXwKIEpebjFklhkg4xlj1cXx8FXxxx0VZiQA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5774034989233623742">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensi</span>
  <span id="freeText5774034989233623742" style="display:none">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensic Academy, he visited the Body Farm in Tennessee. This last commission was the inspiration behind the internationally bestselling The Chemistry of Death, which was shortlisted for the CWA's Duncan Lawrie Dagger and has been translated into 21 languages. Simon Beckett is married and lives in Sheffield. The author of six novels, his second David Hunter thriller, Written in Bone, is published as a Bantam paperback in April 2008.</span>
